# Ads Modifier | Character Animation System Docs

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ads-modifier#overview)

Overview


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Ads Modifier** is used to procedurally aim down sights.

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1519747473-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FrZsugF4ifwEvaFE7BvLB%252Fuploads%252F7ofEx0IX5lwjTv8myc0I%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D45a25c05-f40c-437a-9d0b-0f89059c08b0&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=db3347c7&sv=2)

#### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ads-modifier#inputs)

Inputs

*   **Aim Point** is a transform that will be aligned with your camera. It's possible to bind an external value to this property (e.g., aim point transform provided by the weapon).
    
*   **Is Aiming** defines if the aiming or not. It's recommended to bind here a value from a player controller or a weapon.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ads-modifier#bones)

Bones

*   **Weapon Bone** is the bone will be translated and rotated to align sights with the camera. By default, it's set to **IK weapon\_bone**.
    
*   **Hip Target Bone** is a bone that will be used to compute additive aiming. By default, it's set to the **IK weapon\_bone\_r**.
    
*   **Aim Target Bone** is a bone will be used as an aiming target. Usually, it is a camera socket attached to the head.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ads-modifier#a-ds-blends)

ADS Blends

*   **Position**/**Rotation Blend** Blend between absolute and additive aiming.
    
*   **Aiming Speed**: Playrate of the aiming transition.
    
*   **Aiming Ease Mode**: Interpolation function for the aiming transition.
    
*   **Aim Point Speed**: Speed of changing the aim point transform.
    
*   **Aim Point Ease Mode**: Interpolation function for the aim point transition.
    
*   **Camera Blend**: If set to 0, the weapon will be moved to aim down sights. If set to 1, the camera will be moved instead.
    

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ads-modifier#use-cases)

Use-cases


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This modifier is commonly used for aiming down sights (ADS). There are 2 types of aiming:

1.  **Absolute**: completely overrides the base pose, keeping the sights always aligned.
    
2.  **Additive**: applies on top of the base pose, keeping the animations, but not always aligning sights.
    

Using blend values for different translation and rotation axes can give a nice effect when playing animations in the ADS mode.

circle-check

**Tip**: For example, when playing a reload animation, it is necessary to propagate some motion to the aiming pose — adjusting blend factors will help with that.

[PreviousIK Motionschevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ik-motions)
[NextSway Modifierchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier)

Last updated 3 months ago

*   [Overview](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ads-modifier#overview)
    
*   [Use-cases](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ads-modifier#use-cases)

---

# Sway Modifier | Character Animation System Docs

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier#overview)

Overview


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Sway Modifier** is used to dynamic weapon translation and angular offset when aiming and moving.

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1519747473-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FrZsugF4ifwEvaFE7BvLB%252Fuploads%252F2QG0evWrqPpJOum4aTyX%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd1617b04-ded3-4a89-bcd9-466010b49d50&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=da1f60c5&sv=2)

#### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier#bones)

Bones

*   **Weapon Bone** is the bone that will be animated.
    
*   **Weapon Additive Bone** is an option bone that contains additive motion. This can be useful if you want to apply movement animations
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier#inputs)

Inputs

*   **Delta Look Input** is the delta look input of the player.
    
*   **Move Input** is the movement direction input property.
    
*   **Is Aiming** adjusts values if player is aiming.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier#spring-sway)

Spring Sway

*   **Movement**/**Aiming Sway**
    
    *   **Position**/**Rotation**
        
        *   **Damping**: Oscillation suppression factor in range \[0;1\].
            
        *   **Stiffness**: Oscillation factor in range \[0;1\].
            
        *   **Speed**: Interpolation speed.
            
        *   **Scale**: Final value multiplier.
            
        
    *   **Damping Factor**: How fast sway will interpolate to zero.
        
    *   **Space**: The space sway will be applied in.
        
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier#curve-animation)

Curve Animation

*   **Space Offset** transfroms the additive animation from a custom space.
    
*   **Ads Curve Scale** controls the influence of additive animations when aiming.
    
    *   **Ads Curve Smoothing** is interpolation
        
    

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier#use-cases)

Use-cases


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

While the most common application is the weapon sway effect, this modifier can also be used to animate other parts of the body.

circle-check

**Tip**: For example, it can be used to animate hands or even a character's spine when moving around.

When it comes to adjusting the values, here are the general recommendations:

1.  Damping factor should be around ~0.4-0.5 — this has proved to be more natural in practice.
    
2.  Stiffness should be a bit higher than Damping, around ~0.6-0.7 — this will add that spring or jiggle effect to the sway.
    
3.  Speed depends on how fast the effect should happen. Setting different values for position and rotation might add variety to the motion and make it feel less "procedural".
    
4.  Space should be set to "Component" most of the time. "Bone" might be useful if you want to take the bone's rotation into account.
    

[PreviousAds Modifierchevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ads-modifier)
[NextWeapon Collisionchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/weapon-collision)

Last updated 3 months ago

*   [Overview](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier#overview)
    
*   [Use-cases](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier#use-cases)

---

# Procedural Animation Setup | Character Animation System Docs

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/quickstart/procedural-animation-setup#overview)

Overview


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Procedural Animation Settings** is a data asset created after the setup:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1519747473-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FrZsugF4ifwEvaFE7BvLB%252Fuploads%252FeaNQSPpEfZMvEmj5JtCq%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7c76f155-450e-45a1-9541-a03ed7364913&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=3844b3b0&sv=2)

Animation Modifiers.

It has a "**PA\_**" prefix, which stands for procedural animation:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1519747473-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FrZsugF4ifwEvaFE7BvLB%252Fuploads%252FIOm27Ke0qrsdFZZ0d16D%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D37823fa8-c638-4a35-a045-89b23ab0cc8c&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=307d7725&sv=2)

This asset contains all procedural animation features that will be used for this weapon. It's possible to reorder, remove and add new modifiers. To find out more about procedural animation and modifiers, see:

[🔸Procedural Animationchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/character-animation-system/procedural-animation)

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/quickstart/procedural-animation-setup#fps-animation-modifiers)

FPS Animation Modifiers


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The order of modifiers plays an important role — it defines how procedural features will be created and updated at runtime.

The general structure of Procedural Animation Settings can be split into 3 parts:

1.  Animate IK bones.
    
2.  Apply modifiers (e.g., recoil, sway, ads, etc.).
    
3.  Apply IK to animate character arms and legs, using IK bones as targets.
    

This setup preserves the original animation pose (e.g., reload animation), and lets modify that pose with procedural features.

### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/quickstart/procedural-animation-setup#animating-ik-bones)

Animating IK Bones

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1519747473-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FrZsugF4ifwEvaFE7BvLB%252Fuploads%252FdCRkyN9eMmmvqm8WNDq9%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df1843b4d-4617-4ecb-a3bf-c53ecb0309dd&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9239fe8d&sv=2)

Copy Bones.

[FPS Copy Bones](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/fps-copy-bones)
 positions the weapon bone and hands IK targets.

[Copy Right and Left Foot IK](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/character-animation-system/animation-modifiers/copy-bone)
 copy position and rotation from right and left foot bones to the respective IK targets for feet.

[Attach Left Hand](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/attach-hand)
 is used to apply grip attachments, so the hand is correctly positioned relative to weapon.

### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/quickstart/procedural-animation-setup#applying-procedural-features)

Applying Procedural Features

#### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/quickstart/procedural-animation-setup#offsets)

Offsets

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1519747473-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FrZsugF4ifwEvaFE7BvLB%252Fuploads%252FiSggJQBUOUL236weLwVn%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D69bf463a-5b54-4fdb-8256-08c19b31a131&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=75e0370&sv=2)

All theses modifiers serve one purpose - position the weapon and hands.

*   **FP Offsets** positions weapon and hands in first-person view.
    
*   **TP Offset** positions weapon and hands in third-person view.
    
*   **TP Rest Offset** is applied when the player is in third-person and not aiming.
    

circle-info

**Note**: All this modifiers are based on [FPS Copy Bones](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/fps-copy-bones)
.

It's possible to control the influence of each modifier with **Weight Overrides**:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1519747473-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FrZsugF4ifwEvaFE7BvLB%252Fuploads%252FsZuKSqnfj4HSBaxEE1kd%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D450f7c98-6c5a-49e1-810a-74e10ada54c7&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=72e3e35e&sv=2)

Weight Overrides.

This functionality lets activate any animation modifier when needed. In the FPS Addon Demo, it's used to apply different offsets depending on the aiming state and active perspective.

To find out more about **Weight Overrides**, see: [Weight Overrides](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/character-animation-system/animation-modifiers#weight-overrides)
.

#### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/quickstart/procedural-animation-setup#fps-features)

FPS Features

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1519747473-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FrZsugF4ifwEvaFE7BvLB%252Fuploads%252FFrOAbSYTXvxOEJn1jkxv%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0f76ceea-7aa9-4df9-b4d0-96a8197f3fc0&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=904958be&sv=2)

*   [Ads Modifier](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ads-modifier)
     is used to align sights with the camera.
    
*   [Sway Modifier](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/sway-modifier)
     applies aiming and movement sway, as well as additive animations (idle and movement).
    
*   [Procedural Recoil](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/recoil-animation)
     applies firing animations.
    
*   [IK Motion](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/modifiers/ik-motions)
     applies dynamic additive animations, which are used for aiming, draw and holster motions.
    

circle-check

**Tip**: Aiming modifier is applied first, so sway and recoil effects can be applied on top of it.

### 

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/fps-addon/quickstart/procedural-animation-setup#general-modifiers)

General Modifiers

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1519747473-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FrZsugF4ifwEvaFE7BvLB%252Fuploads%252FgmxeyTWwb1RU8rnPFxAe%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7959b825-8cf4-406f-8f47-5a8136f9d209&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=96b45dd6&sv=2)

*   [**Movement Turns**](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/character-animation-system/animation-modifiers/pivot-modifier)
     adds leaning when moving around.
    
*   [**Look Modifier**](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/character-animation-system/animation-modifiers/look-modifier)
     applies look rotation and turn in place effects.
    
*   [**Step Modifier**](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/character-animation-system-docs/character-animation-system/animation-modifiers/step-modifier)
     plays procedural step animations to avoid feet sliding.

 modifiers.

What is Motion Warping?


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

_Motion Warping_ is advanced animation technology, used to adjust character root motion in runtime.

This plugin allows your characters to climb and vault over obstacles, enter vehicles, finish off enemies and much more!

circle-check

**Tip:** make sure to join our [Discord](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/)

# Introduction | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/introduction#what-is-animation-warping)

What is animation warping?


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Animation or motion warping is used to procedurally align your character with targets in world space. In games, it's very often used for climbing, vaulting, melee combat and even vehicles.

The main goal of warping is simple: re-use character animation for different obstacles, enemy positions, etc.

circle-info

**Example:** let's say you have a climbing animation, that was made for a one meter high object. Obviously, this animation will not work with a two meter high obstacle. Motion Warping plugin makes it possible, by procedurally adjusting your character animation.

circle-check

**Tip:** thanks to this technology, you can save hundreds of animation clips, by applying the same motion for different gameplay scenarios.

In the next section, you will learn in detail of how our Motion Warping plugin works.

[PreviousWelcome!chevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity)
[NextHow this asset workschevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works)

Last updated 1 year ago

---

# Warp Providers | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/warp-providers#technical-aspects)

Technical Aspects


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Warp Providers** are components that provide active interaction with target points.

circle-check

**Example**: the built-in **MantleComponent** will search for the climbable obstacle point, and then pass it to the _Motion Warping_ component.

This plugin offers a common interface - **IWarpProvider** \- that can be used to create custom _Warp Providers_. This interface contains a single method called **Interact** that returns the result of a check:

WarpProviderInterface.cs

Copy

    public struct WarpInteractionResult
    {
        public WarpPoint[] points;            // Target points.
        public MotionWarpingAsset asset;      // Warping asset with settings.      
        public bool success;                  // If the interaction can be started.
    
        public bool IsValid()
        {
            return success && points != null && asset != null;
        }
    }
        
    public interface IWarpPointProvider
    {
        public WarpInteractionResult Interact(GameObject instigator);
    }

The plugin supports both moving and static obstacles out of the box. Here is how to correctly pass the data for each obstacle type:

chevron-rightMoving obstacles[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/warp-providers#moving-obstacles)

To make the **Warp Point** depend on a specific transform, make sure to specify that target transform, and convert the point world coordinates to that transform's space:

chevron-rightStatic obstacles[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/warp-providers#static-obstacles)

If you want the **Warp Point** to be static in world space, make sure to pass the world coordinates of the desired interaction point:

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/warp-providers#example)

Example


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here is how to use a **Warp Provider** in code. We are going to use **VaultComponent** in this example:

It is also possible to pass the _gameObject_ as a parameter in the Interact method:

In this case, the **Motion Warping** will try to get the first component that implements the **IWarpProvider** interface and interact with it.

[PreviousMotion Warping Componentchevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-component)
[NextMotion Warping IKchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-ik)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Technical Aspects](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/warp-providers#technical-aspects)
    
*   [Example](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/warp-providers#example)
    

Copy

    result.points = new[]
    {
        new WarpPoint()
        {
            transform = hit.transform,
            position = hit.transform.InverseTransformPoint(_targetPosition),
            rotation = Quaternion.Inverse(hit.transform.rotation) * _targetRotation
        }
    };

Copy

    result.points = new[]
    {
        new WarpPoint()
        {
            position = _targetPosition,
            rotation = _targetRotation
        }
    };

Copy

    public class YourController : MonoBehaviour
    {
        //...
        private MotionWarping _warpingComponent;
        //...
        
        //...
        private VaultComponent _vaultComponent;
        //...
    
        private void Start()
        {
            //...
            _warpingComponent = GetComponent<MotionWarping>();
            //...
        }
            
        private void Update()
        {
            if (Input.GetKeyDown(KeyCode.F))
            {
                _warpingComponent.Interact(_vaultComponent);
            }
        }
        
        //...
    }

Copy

    _warpingComponent.Interact(gameObject);

# Motion Warping Component | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-component#in-the-editor)

In the Editor


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Motion Warping** is the main component in the system, as it is used for initiating interactions and warping animations in runtime. Make sure to add this component to your character:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FE3tVZ0OAhZycsQjaO2iS%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dfe37b053-e941-49b1-b565-f75ad50b670c&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d56250a0&sv=2)

Example of a set up Motion Warping component.

Let's break down each property of this component:

*   **Scale Play Rate**: whether to modify the original play rate; for example, if the distance is longer - the play rate will be reduced, if shorter - increased.
    
*   **Play Animator**: whether to automatically play the animation via _Animator_.
    
*   **Blend Time**: cross-fade blend in time for the animation.
    
*   **OnWarpStarted**: called right before the interaction. Use it to disable collisions and other systems.
    
*   **OnWarpEnded**: called right after the interaction. Use it to enable collision or movement.
    

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-component#in-code)

In Code


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

It is important to reference the **Motion Warping** component in your controller code:

We will use this component to start interactions. And more about that in the next chapter!

[PreviousMotion Warping Assetchevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-asset)
[NextWarp Providerschevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/warp-providers)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [In the Editor](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-component#in-the-editor)

Copy

    public class YourController : MonoBehaviour
    {
        //...

        //...

        {
            //...

            //...

    }

# How this asset works | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#how-does-it-warp-the-motion)

How does it warp the motion?


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Our plugin uses 4 concepts in order to properly adjust character animation in realtime:

1.  [Warping Phases](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#warping-phases)
    
2.  [Play Rate Scale](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#play-rate-scale)
    
3.  [Total Root Motion](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#total-root-motion)
    
4.  [Post-Animation Update](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#post-animation-update)
    

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#warping-phases)

Warping Phases


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Warping Phases** are segments of the animation, where we want to perfrorm warping. In our plugin, these are **purple** draggable windows found in the [Motion Warping Asset](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-asset)
:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252Fgez1NwAzeUdfQBUaeWgK%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db04b7ac9-efff-4341-b5d7-9cf8643028be&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=e4b9d7c7&sv=2)

Vaulting animation example.

The example above is a vaulting animation that has 3 warping windows. **But why 3?** The amount of warping windows depends on the number of target points we are going to provide. To vault over an object, we must know:

*   Front obstacle edge point
    
*   Rear obstacle edge point
    
*   Landing point
    

This makes it 3 warping points, which gives us 3 animation segments.

circle-info

**Another example:** climbing animation - we only need a single warp phase, because we want to go from the current character position to the obstacle top point.

**Warping Phases** also contain useful information about the animation segment, such as:

*   Target point position and rotation offset
    
*   Segment play rate controls
    
*   Segment start and end time
    

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252F7DWsoXI3HWTxsaUtBmxc%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D699c08b8-84e7-4f63-b174-fb34f3b46e20&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=fa867435&sv=2)

**T and R Offsets** are used to offset the target point of the segment. This is super useful since the system will always align the character root with the target point. You can also use this to fix awkward poses, caused by the original animation.

**Min and Max playrate** define the play rate limitations. You will find out more about the play rate in the next chapter.

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#play-rate-scale)

Play Rate Scale


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When warping animations, we might run into a situation when the obstacle is simply too long. If we keep the play rate the same, it will look strange, as if the character has an insane momentum.

To fix this, our plugin scales the play rate for the current animation phase. This is done by computing the vector length difference.

circle-info

**Example:** if the obstacle is 1m away, and our animation was made for a 0.5m obstacle, the play rate will be scaled down twice: from 1 to 0.5. If it was 0.25m away, the play rate will be increased from 1 to 2.

You can adjust the play rate for any segment manually by editing the respective values:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FBJv23dCQZ1VRVOk7OSCN%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Ddffd73c6-074e-4803-9e8b-633bda9b2d5e&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=3b951986&sv=2)

The play rate is finally applied in the **Animator Controller** via a float parameter:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FeucTCGSUxnvA01hwyWwm%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da695ce4b-a698-4b2a-b2ea-43f414a08a3f&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=7ae25081&sv=2)

If you have a custom animation system, you will need to find a way to manually plug in the adjusted play rate value.

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#total-root-motion)

Total Root Motion


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Every **Warping Phase** contains accumulated root motion for each translation axis.

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FGhpV3fjZahGUiBeUVvVH%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D68c73e63-4739-4d87-b806-8c155de5bfbb&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=648c76e1&sv=2)

circle-check

**Tip:** the total root motion is refreshed when you re-open the motion warping asset.

But why is it important? This feature is used to preserve the original motion. This is crucial for proper warping, and you will find out more in the next chapter.

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#post-animation-update)

Post-Animation Update


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Animations are warped in the `**LateUpdate()**`, right after the Animator update. This allows to completely take over the character root motion, and preserve the previously applied IK and constraints.

To warp the motion, we must know the difference between the original animation and the desired target point. Let's use a climbing animation curve as an example:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FmnQ2BJdTYBc6R0lb55tw%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7aeabd03-c30f-4858-919b-a8f9b9a873cd&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6110047&sv=2)

Climbing animation curve

This curve offsets the character's vertical position by ~3 meters. The Total Root Motion will be ~3, as it's the final offset.

In runtime, when our animation is playing, the system will accumulate animation translation deltas, and divide them by the **Total Root Motion.**

circle-check

**Example:** let's say our animation was made for climbing a 3-meter obstacle. The object we want to climb is 6 meters, and we desire to warp. The height delta is 3 meters, so we need to add it to the current root motion, using total root motion:

**Formula: offset = desiredHeightDelta \* accumulatedRootMotion / totalRootMotion,**

where **(accumulatedRootMotion / totalRootMotion)** is in the range \[0;1\] and acts as an alpha or weight.

After that, **Motion Warping** will apply the offset to the current position.

circle-info

**Note:** rotation warping is slightly different. Instead of using Total Root Motion, rotations are simply SLERP'ed based on the current Warp Phase normalized time:

**rotation = Quaternion.Slerp(startRotation, targetRotation, normalizedTime).**

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#post-scriptum)

Post Scriptum


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In the next section, you will be able to apply this knowledge in practice! If you have any questions about the system, feel free to join our [**Discord**arrow-up-right](https://discord.gg/kinemation-1027338787958816860)
 community.

[PreviousIntroductionchevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/introduction)
[NextMotion Warping Assetchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-asset)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [How does it warp the motion?](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#how-does-it-warp-the-motion)
    
*   [Warping Phases](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#warping-phases)
    
*   [Play Rate Scale](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works#play-rate-scale)

# Motion Warping Asset | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-asset#curves-and-warp-phases)

Curves and Warp Phases


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This plugin uses **Motion Warping Assets** to control how the animation will be warped in runtime. To create a new **Motion Warping Asset**, make sure to: **Right click -> Create -> MotionWarping -> MotionWarpingAsset.**

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FSa4AvsrwA6fmjFadVu0K%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D91fa79a7-20bd-4b98-84ff-396b87af3723&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=39baf959&sv=2)

This asset contains all properties that configure the warping process.

Now we need to select the animation we want to warp. Let's use a **JumpOver** clip as an example. Then, press the **"Extract Curves"** button. It will generate the root motion curves from the clip:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FeMjD1dYPb2zKskUWTdkv%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1d8791c4-36bc-4d75-a4bb-d6df873beaea&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=b77e8410&sv=2)

Curves are properly extracted!

circle-check

**Tip**: you can modify these curves manually if your animation does not contain keyframes for the root.

The next step is to tell the system what parts of the animation we want to warp. To do this, we need to set the **Phases Amount** to the number of parts we want to warp.

circle-info

**Example:** In the **JumpOver** animation, this value is **3** because we have 3 target points: close edge, far edge, and landing point.

After that, hit the **"Generate Phases"** button:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252Fgez1NwAzeUdfQBUaeWgK%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db04b7ac9-efff-4341-b5d7-9cf8643028be&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=e4b9d7c7&sv=2)

circle-check

**Tip**: it is possible to drag and resize **Warp Phases**, by hovering over the green bars and their edges.

For every green segment, there is an element in the **Warp Phases** list. Let's see what properties the phases have:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252F9m6Swy3nG9c2Gzd5JOBM%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0f94b686-9ecf-41d3-8e73-77c2528f5cf1&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=570cc723&sv=2)

*   **T Offset**: translation offset for the target point.
    
*   **R Offset**: rotation offset for the target point.
    
*   **Start Time**: animation start time for this segment.
    
*   **End Time**: animation end time for this segment.
    
*   **Min Rate**: minimum allowed playrate.
    
*   **Max Rate**: maximum allowed playrate.
    
*   **Total Root Motion**: the final distance for each axis.
    

circle-exclamation

**Tip:** close and open up the asset again to generate the total root motion!

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-asset#additional-properties)

Additional Properties


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For fine-tuning, **Motion Warping Asset** offers additional functionality to control the warping process:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FQ9mcwjh3nXMsovkOqEKF%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D81621e48-e859-4767-95b1-5dd9df319450&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=402812a1&sv=2)

*   **Use Linear:** whether to use linear interpolation for the selected axes.
    
*   **Use Animation:** whether to play animation on top of warping adjustments; keep this on for all axes, unless animation is not required.
    
*   **Use Warping**: whether to warp the selected axes.
    
*   **Use Collision**: whether to use native (_CharacterController_ or _Rigidbody_) collision when warping. For example: if we want to warp the sword attack animation, we can enable the collision, so the character will react to the environment.
    

* * *

At this point, our **Motion Warping Asset** is ready. Next, we are going to learn about the main component of the system.

[PreviousHow this asset workschevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/concept/how-this-asset-works)
[NextMotion Warping Componentchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-component)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Curves and Warp Phases](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-asset#curves-and-warp-phases)
    
*   [Additional Properties](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-asset#additional-properties)

# Mantle Component | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/mantle-component#overview)

Overview


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This component is used to climb obstacles. Add it directly to your character:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FFXw5rJcCtIINED09vTZK%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D446b3b11-6fb4-4ca4-a315-947be9c283d5&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=a7ea5f41&sv=2)

Inspector

**Mantle High** - _Motion Warping Asset_ for climbing high obstcales.

**Mantle Low** - _Motion Warping Asset_ for climbing low obstacles.

**Settings** is a _Data Asset_, which defines the settings for climbing:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FL5FoUtBwEoRo7elhdiEN%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df0843906-f139-4c24-85e5-247ca818dea5&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=61f9d4e7&sv=2)

Mantle Settings.

circle-check

**Tip:** you can create Mantle Settings and Motion Warping Assets by right clicking **Create/KINEMATION/Motion Warping/**

*   **Layer Maks:** defines the collision mask.
    
*   **Max Height:** maximum allowed height. If obstacle's height is greater than this value, climbing won't be performed.
    
*   **Low Height:** required height to use high-climbing asset. If the obstacle height is great than this value, the system will use the Climb High Asset.
    
*   **Min Height:** minimum allowed height. If obstacle's height is less than this value, climbing won't be performed.
    
*   **Max Distance:** max allowed distance between the character and obstacle.
    
*   **Capsule Radius/Height:** parameters for character capsule trace. It will be used to find the obstacle and check if the obstacle's edge has enough space to place the character.
    
*   **Sphere Edge Check Radius:** defines radius for sphere trace, which will be used to find obstales edge.
    
*   **Max Surface Incline Angle:** defines the maximum allowed surface incline angle.
    
*   **Forward Offset:** defines the forward offset from the target point.
    

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/mantle-component#how-does-it-work)

How does it work?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To initiate an interaction, make sure to get a reference to the **MantleComponent** in your code. Then, use the **Interact** method of the **MotionWarping** component:

**MantleComponent** uses 3 stages to deteremine the target obstacle point:

1.  Try to find the obstacle using the **Capsule** properties and **Max Distance**.
    
2.  Try to find the edge by using **Sphere Check** properties, max and min obstacle height properties.
    
3.  Check if point has enough space for the character.
    

If all steps return true, the system will begin interaction.

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/mantle-component#motion-waring-asset-requirements)

Motion Waring Asset Requirements


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Usually climbing is about going from A to B, so make sure to have only 1 Warp Phase in your asset:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252F78SVKxQnZwmTa6ve5o5F%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2f33d188-556d-421b-8202-3d04ded218e5&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=8faef16&sv=2)

[PreviousMotion Warping IKchevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/motion-warping-ik)
[NextVault Componentchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/vault-component)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Overview](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/mantle-component#overview)
    
*   [How does it work?](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/mantle-component#how-does-it-work)
    
*   [Motion Waring Asset Requirements](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/mantle-component#motion-waring-asset-requirements)
    

Copy

    _warping.Interact(_mantleComponent);

# Motion Warping IK | Motion Warping for Unity

**Motion Warping** has an **IK Locking feature**. It is used to prevent feet/hands from sliding during actions, which can be useful if the warped animation exceeds the range of the original motion.

It is very easy to add and use this feature, make sure to add this component first:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FWFeMTHPkA4yR6caojqyH%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D800e0014-3a18-4e97-b4c5-087ab9ab3c62&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=6b85b4bb&sv=2)

Motion Warping Ik component.

**Component Weight** defines the global weight for IK. You can disable it by setting the value to zero.

The IK Component includes 4 Lock States: for each hand and foot. Let's break down the properties:

*   **Control Curve Name**: the name of the float parameter in your Animator Controller, which will control the IK weight for this bone.
    
*   **Bone Reference**: the tip bone, usually it's a hand or a foot.
    
*   **Interp Speed**: smoothing for IK blending in/out.
    

Make sure to add these new parameters to your **Animator Controller**:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FmKzteFX7W6p5qsaDLhbZ%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D955ff877-2ca1-4777-9bfd-26181ea56a00&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=3f436469&sv=2)

You can choose different names.

Then, make sure to assign the proper parameter names in the **Motion Warping Ik** component.

Now you need to add curves to your animations, to enable and disable IK. Let's take this vaulting animation as an example:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252Fuv6JdWc8vXXjCnWmz2iQ%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D18af2f3f-d8d4-4428-b698-554e72ebcd3b&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=1c5e5cbf&sv=2)

This animation only locks the left hand.

In this case, we want to lock the left foot when it touches the surface of the obstacle. Let's take a closer look at the curve:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FojJxpR21N9UL5i5PgxGN%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df4799837-a7d2-4c62-a84b-7953a684e46c&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=198299a7&sv=2)

Use a CONSTANT interpolation.

Make sure the curve value changes instantly, you can do this by **right-clicking** on the key and selecting the constant option:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FO5trySVbHwyBV0xkaGx5%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df2dc6369-ed94-499b-a7b6-fe8863a57f43&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=4028367d&sv=2)

And that's pretty much it! As you can see, the process is quite straightforward, and you can leverage this feature to improve the quality of your animations.

[PreviousWarp Providerschevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/fundametals/warp-providers)
[NextMantle Componentchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/mantle-component)

Last updated 1 year ago

# Roll Component | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/roll-component#overview)

Overview


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This component is used to move the character forward. Perfect for Sliding or Rolling mechanics. Make sure to add it directly to your character:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FNJHjMeGeFuQ3M290O4CQ%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db0120158-858b-4e1b-91f1-66d3fb8a6110&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=448b6ad&sv=2)

Inspector.

*   **Capsule Height/Radius:** used for capsule trace to find an obstacle.
    
*   **Layer Mask:** used to filter collision targets.
    
*   **Rolling Asset:** Motion Warping Asset with rolling animation.
    
*   **Roll Max/Min Distance:** max/min allowed movement distance.
    
*   **Max Fall Off:** max allowed vertical offset for the target point.
    

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/roll-component#how-does-it-work)

How does it work?


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This component uses 2 stages to trace down the target point:

1.  Try to find a blocking obstacle in the way. If an obstacle found, abort the interaction.
    
2.  Trace down to find a target point. If no hit, stop the interaction.
    

After that the interaction will be initiated.

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/roll-component#motion-warping-asset-requirements)

Motion Warping Asset Requirements


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Only 1 Warping Phase is required for this component to work properly.

[PreviousLand Componentchevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/land-component)
[NextAlign Componentchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/align-component)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Overview](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/roll-component#overview)
    
*   [How does it work?](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/roll-component#how-does-it-work)
    
*   [Motion Warping Asset Requirements](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/roll-component#motion-warping-asset-requirements)

# Align Component | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/align-component#overview)

Overview


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This component is used for melee combat and interactions. Add it to the object you want your character to interact with (enemy character, car, etc.):

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FboYiqhmAaPEYWGRUWUwy%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D950fd1a6-c911-4d2a-a7f0-5aec4043baa9&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=75cf431&sv=2)

Align Component.

**Interaction Angle:** defines the max allowed interaction angle. The system will use the Game Object forward axis.

**Offset Angle:** yaw rotation offset for the Interaction Angle.

**Distance:** max allowed interaction distance.

**Target Anim Name:** name of the animation to play for the object player will interact with. For example: enemy character, car, door, etc.

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/align-component#how-does-it-work)

How does it work?


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are multiple ways to use **Align Component**, but the most popular one is to get a reference to the interaction target object. For example, let's say that we enter collision box for a car. Now we can use the car Game Object as a paramter in the Interact method:

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/align-component#motion-warping-asset-requirements)

Motion Warping Asset Requirements


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This component only requires 1 **Warp Phase** to work properly, as the character will go from the current to the target position.

[PreviousRoll Componentchevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/roll-component)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Overview](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/align-component#overview)
    
*   [How does it work?](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/align-component#how-does-it-work)
    
*   [Motion Warping Asset Requirements](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/align-component#motion-warping-asset-requirements)
    

Copy

    private void OnTriggerEnter(Collider other)
    {
        _interactionTarget = other.gameObject;
    }
    
    private void OnTriggerExit(Collider other)
    {
        _interactionTarget = null;
    }
    
    private void TryInteracting()
    {
        _warping.Interact(_interactionTarget);    
    }

# Vault Component | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/vault-component#overview)

Overview


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This component is used to vault over obstacles. Add it directly to your character:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FyBsrvYJnK0yaYyjUlokn%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Daacbca59-833b-4f6d-82a7-f0e771aa8975&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9e6f3055&sv=2)

Inspector.

circle-check

**Tip:** you can create Mantle Settings and Motion Warping Assets by right clicking **Create/KINEMATION/Motion Warping/**

**Vaulting Settings** define properties to vault over obstacles:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FHWxOlwUXjdhhDfozB8bD%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1cb57bc8-1c4e-48b3-a6d4-ad6da3340679&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=cc38f47&sv=2)

Vaulting Settings.

*   **Layer Mask:** defines the collision mask.
    
*   **Capsule Radius:** radius for capsule trace.
    
*   **Max/Min Obstacle Length:** max and min allowed lengths of the obstacle.
    
*   **Sphere Edge Check Radius:** sphere trace radius to find the edges of the obstacle.
    
*   **Max Allowed Start Length:** max allowed distance between the front edge and the character.
    
*   **Max/Min Allowed Start Height:** max/min allowed height of the fron edge.
    
*   **Close Edge Deviation:** edge vertical offset.
    
*   **Far Edge Offset:** start vertical offset to find the rear edge.
    
*   **Max/Min Allowed End Height:** max/min allowed height of the rear edge.
    

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/vault-component#how-does-it-work)

How does it work?


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The **VaultComponent** uses 3 stages to find all target points: Close Edge, Far Edge and End Point.

1.  Try to find an obstacle and the Close Edge.
    
2.  Try to find the End Point.
    
3.  Try to find the Far Edge
    

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/vault-component#motion-warping-asset-requirements)

Motion Warping Asset Requirements


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Vaulting over animation must have 3 Warp Phases.

1.  Go from current point to the Close Edge.
    
2.  Go from the Close Edge to the Far Edge.
    
3.  Go from the Far Edge to the End Point.
    

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FCaXLu63ky0PedGL12fMe%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D5aa09829-4695-421b-95f5-57cd8147e772&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=b7985c8a&sv=2)

[PreviousMantle Componentchevron-left](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/mantle-component)
[NextLand Componentchevron-right](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/land-component)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Overview](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/vault-component#overview)
    
*   [How does it work?](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/vault-component#how-does-it-work)

# Land Component | Motion Warping for Unity

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/land-component#overview)

Overview


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This component is used to distance-match landing animations with the ground point. Make sure to add it to your character:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252FSDBDFxGkJySBtTt4cKCy%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0000384e-7c6a-4dc3-ae89-06005ee1a9a3&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=bf7648df&sv=2)

Land Component Inspector.

Unlike other components, this one does not use a Data Asset, so you can configure everything directly in the component.

*   **Hard Landing:** Motion Warping Asset for high vertical velocity landing.
    
*   **Soft Landing:** Motion Warping Asset for low vertical velocity landing.
    
*   **Hard Landing Height:** defines max allowed height.
    
*   **Soft Landing Height:** if character's vertical height is greater than this value, Hard Landing animation will be used.
    
*   **Min Allowed Height:** minimum allowed height.
    
*   **Capsule Radius:** capsule trace radius.
    
*   **Forward Offset:** defines the forward offset upon landing.
    
*   **Layer Mask:** collision mask.
    

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/land-component#how-does-it-work)

How does it work?


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This component will use a raycast to check if there's a possible ground to land. Then the interaction will start.

[hashtag](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/components/land-component#motion-warping-asset-requirements)

Motion Warping Asset Requirements


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use a single **Warp Phase**:

![](https://kinemation.gitbook.io/motion-warping-for-unity/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1415000928-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUAC5B06XWM8YyqQzyIP2%252Fuploads%252F78SVKxQnZwmTa6ve5o5F%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2f33d188-556d-421b-8202-3d04ded218e5&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=8faef16&sv=2)
